What's really interesting is seeing the difference between the real speed on the GPS dash and the apparent speed shown by the car itself. It's not showing the real speed, as it were. The in-car reading is inaccurate to begin with, which means at any given point it's about 5% above the real speed of the car. But when you're braking, it's actually a couple tenths BEHIND in updating the information. So for example, at 4:25 , the real speed of the car is 164 km/h. But the in-car dash is showing 177km/h. That's a pretty substantial difference, and an indication of a serious issue in the software.

I am a fan of Tesla and the Model S, but let's be honest: it is not made to race on a track.  On one hand, it is incredible that a 2200 kg car manages 7:35.58. It achieves this through ridiculous linear accelleration, but rather poor curve performance. OK, it is a few sec faster than the Porsche Taycan (7:42). But if you consider the immense power (1020 PS) of the Model S Plaid, I think this result is not that impressive.  Consider this: A Porsche 911 Carrera S (992) has less than half the power (450 PS) and runs the NÃ¼rburgring in 7:30.00.  Even more impressive: a Megane IV Trophy R with less than 1/3 the power (300 PS) and only front wheel drive runs the ring in 7:40.10 (just 5 sec slower!).
This car with over 1000hp was still slower than an Audi RS3 family sedan that's half the cost and has nearly 1/3 the hp. I can respect EV for being the grocery getter replacement but as of now they are no replacement for real sports cars - especially on a track.

Professional race drivers have got to hate this.  Part of the experience is the noise that goes with the drive.  With no engine noise to enhance the audible signal cues as to when to start braking or accelerating per corner, it takes away 1 of the senses that drivers rely on.  It is all part of the "feel" of driving a machine.  There is no argument that fast is fast, but to truly be using all your trained senses to control a machine, audible noises have to be a part of it.

Tesla is 20 years behind top established car makers in terms of driving dynamics and chassis development.
